   <span class="pl-k">break</span>
 <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Boo!'</span>)
 <span class="pl-s1">goblins</span> <span class="pl-c1">-=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'That was scary!'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer: the following:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="2 witches!
3 witches!
4 witches!
7 zombies!
5 zombies!
3 zombies!
Boo!
Boo!
Boo!
That was scary!"><pre class="notranslate"><code>2 witches!
3 witches!
4 witches!
7 zombies!
5 zombies!
3 zombies!
Boo!
Boo!
Boo!
That was scary!
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Why bring this up? Python's <code>range()</code> behaves <em>slightly</em> differently from Haskell's ranges:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Python's <code>range()</code> is semi-open: it includes the first item, but not the last. So, <code>range(2,5) = [2,5) = [2,3,4]</code></li>
<li>Haskell's <code>..</code> is completely closed: <code>2..5 = [2,5] = [2,3,4,5]</code></li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Learning Python through Challenges - Object-Oriented Programming</h2><a id="user-content-learning-python-through-challenges---object-oriented-programming" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Learning Python through Challenges - Object-Oriented Programming" href="#learning-python-through-challenges---object-oriented-programming"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Classes</h3><a id="user-content-classes" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Classes" href="#classes"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Consider the following Python class:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class Car:
  MILES_PER_GAL = 30
  def __init__(self, gallons):
    self.gas_gallons = gallons
    self.odometer = 0

  def drive(self, miles):
    gals_needed = miles / Car.MILES_PER_GAL
    if self.gas_gallons &gt; gals_needed:
      self.gas_gallons -= gals_needed
      self.odometer += miles

  def get_odometer(self):
    return self.odometer"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Car</span>:
  <span class="pl-v">MILES_PER_GAL</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">30</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">gallons</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">gas_gallons</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">gallons</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">odometer</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">drive</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">miles</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">gals_needed</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">miles</span> <span class="pl-c1">/</span> <span class="pl-v">Car</span>.<span class="pl-v">MILES_PER_GAL</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">gas_gallons</span> <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">gals_needed</span>:
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">gas_gallons</span> <span class="pl-c1">-=</span> <span class="pl-s1">gals_needed</span>
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">odometer</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-s1">miles</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">get_odometer</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">odometer</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We can insantiate and use the object like so:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def use_car():
  c1 = Car(16)  # 16 gallons of gas
  c1.drive(10)
  print(f'I drove {c1.get_odometer()} mi')"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">use_car</span>():
  <span class="pl-s1">c1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Car</span>(<span class="pl-c1">16</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># 16 gallons of gas</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">c1</span>.<span class="pl-en">drive</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'I drove <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">c1</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_odometer</span>()<span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> mi'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Looking at this code, can you identify:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>how do you define a constructor in a Python class?</li>
<li>how do you define member variables in a Python class?</li>
<li>how is a method different from a normal Python function?</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>We define a constructor with the <code>__init__</code> function. Notice the "explicit" <code>self</code> - this behaves like <code>this</code> in C++, but is <em>always</em> the first argument!</li>
<li>We can define new member variables by just calling <code>self.[variable_name]</code>! Note that you can't declare variables without assigning them!</li>
<li>We define it "in" the function; it must have a <code>self</code> argument; and, it can access member fields/variables.</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">Now, consider this updated code:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class Car:
  MILES_PER_GAL = 30
  def __init__(self, gallons):
    self.gas_gallons = gallons
    self.odometer = 0

  def drive(self, miles):
    gals_needed = miles / Car.MILES_PER_GAL
    if self.gas_gallons &gt; gals_needed:
      self.gas_gallons -= gals_needed

  def __update_odometer(self, miles):
    self.odometer += miles

  def get_odometer(self):
    return self.odometer"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Car</span>:
  <span class="pl-v">MILES_PER_GAL</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">30</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">gallons</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">gas_gallons</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">gallons</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">odometer</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">drive</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">miles</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">gals_needed</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">miles</span> <span class="pl-c1">/</span> <span class="pl-v">Car</span>.<span class="pl-v">MILES_PER_GAL</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">gas_gallons</span> <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">gals_needed</span>:
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">gas_gallons</span> <span class="pl-c1">-=</span> <span class="pl-s1">gals_needed</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__update_odometer</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">miles</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">odometer</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-s1">miles</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">get_odometer</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">odometer</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">and</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def use_car():
  c1 = Car(16)  # 16 gallons of gas
  c1.drive(10)
  print(f'I drove {c1.get_odometer()} mi')"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">use_car</span>():
  <span class="pl-s1">c1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Car</span>(<span class="pl-c1">16</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># 16 gallons of gas</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">c1</span>.<span class="pl-en">drive</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'I drove <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">c1</span>.<span class="pl-en">get_odometer</span>()<span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> mi'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Three more questions:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Changing <code>get_odometer()</code>'s return statement to <code>return odometer</code> doesn't work --- why?</li>
<li>How do you call a method from another method?</li>
<li>How do we indicate whether a method is public or private?</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answers:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Unlike C++, Python requires an explicit <code>self.</code> to identify member variables.</li>
<li>Again, unlike C++, Python requires an explicit <code>self.</code> to identify member functions.</li>
<li>Python's access modifiers are built into variable names: two underscores creates a private method (compare <code>__update_odometer</code> to <code>get_odometer</code>). Other variables are public by default!</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }
Syntactically, the definition of a Python class is a sequence of statements that gets run anytime the class is instantiated. So, you can include any legal Python code in your class definition!</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Object Allocation</h3><a id="user-content-object-allocation" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Object Allocation" href="#object-allocation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This question has a bit of setup. Compare this C++ code:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="#include &lt;cmath&gt;

class Circle {
public:
  Circle(double rad)
    { this-&gt;rad = rad; }

  double area() const
    { return M_PI * rad * rad; }

  void setRadius(double rad)
    { this-&gt;rad = rad; }

private:
  double rad;
};"><pre>#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>cmath<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Circle</span> {
<span class="pl-k">public:</span>
  <span class="pl-en">Circle</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> rad)
    { <span class="pl-c1">this</span>-&gt;<span class="pl-smi">rad</span> = rad; }

  <span class="pl-k">double</span> <span class="pl-en">area</span>() <span class="pl-k">const</span>
    { <span class="pl-k">return</span> M_PI * rad * rad; }

  <span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">setRadius</span>(<span class="pl-k">double</span> rad)
    { <span class="pl-c1">this</span>-&gt;<span class="pl-smi">rad</span> = rad; }

<span class="pl-k">private:</span>
  <span class="pl-k">double</span> rad;
};</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">with the Python equivalent:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import math

class Circle:
  def __init__(self, rad):
    self.rad = rad

  def area(self):
    return math.pi * self.rad**2

  def set_radius(self, rad):
    self.rad = rad"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">math</span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">area</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">math</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">*</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span><span class="pl-c1">**</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">set_radius</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">rad</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In C++, there are two ways we can define an object:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// on the stack - &quot;no pointer&quot;
Circle c(10);
cout &lt;&lt; c.area();
// on the heap - &quot;with a pointer&quot;
Circle *p = new Circle(20);
cout &lt;&lt; p-&gt;area();"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> on the stack - "no pointer"</span>
Circle <span class="pl-en">c</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>);
cout &lt;&lt; c.area();
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> on the heap - "with a pointer"</span>
Circle *p = <span class="pl-k">new</span> Circle(<span class="pl-c1">20</span>);
cout &lt;&lt; p-&gt;<span class="pl-en">area</span>();</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In Python, we can only do</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="c = Circle(10)
print(c.area())"><pre><span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">area</span>())</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">(Carey's slides then have a long animation that explains how heap versus stack allocation works; this is a refresher from CS32)</p>
<p dir="auto">How does Python allocate objects - is it directly/on-the-stack, or with pointer indirection?</p>
<p dir="auto">Hint:
this is valid code:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="c = Circle(10)
print(c.area())
c = None"><pre><span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">area</span>())
<span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer: Python uses something <em>like</em> pointers, called an <strong>object reference</strong>. Every Python object is allocated on the heap. Unlike C++, we don't use any special syntax to "dereference" a pointer.</p>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }
In Python, <em>all</em> variables are object references. This applies to primitives in other languages, like numbers -- <code>42</code>. On reassignment, we don't "change" the allocated <code>42</code>; instead, we allocate a new number, and point to it. Though, this is mostly abstracted away from you as a programmer!</p>
<p dir="auto">This affects how we call methods too:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Circle class in Python
import math

class Circle:

  def __init__(self, rad):
    self.rad = rad

  def area(self):
    return math.pi * self.rad**2

  def set_radius(self, rad):
    self.rad = rad

c = Circle(10)
print(c.area()) # here, &quot;self&quot; points to c!"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Circle class in Python</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">math</span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>:

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">area</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">math</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">*</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span><span class="pl-c1">**</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">set_radius</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>

<span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">area</span>()) <span class="pl-c"># here, "self" points to c!</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Class Variables</h3><a id="user-content-class-variables" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Class Variables" href="#class-variables"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Consider this module <code>thing.py</code>:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# thing.py
class Thing:
 thing_count = 0

 def __init__(self, v):
  self.value = v
  Thing.thing_count += 1
  self.thing_num = Thing.thing_count"><pre><span class="pl-c"># thing.py</span>
<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>:
 <span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>

 <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">v</span>):
  <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">value</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">v</span>
  <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_num</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">What will the following print? Why?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import thing

t1 = Thing(&quot;a&quot;)
print(f&quot;{t1.thing_num} {Thing.thing_count}&quot;)


t2 = Thing(&quot;b&quot;)
print(f&quot;{t1.thing_num} {Thing.thing_count}&quot;)
print(f&quot;{t2.thing_num} {Thing.thing_count}&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">thing</span>

<span class="pl-s1">t1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>(<span class="pl-s">"a"</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f"<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">t1</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_num</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>"</span>)


<span class="pl-s1">t2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>(<span class="pl-s">"b"</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f"<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">t1</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_num</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>"</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f"<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">t2</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_num</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="1 1
1 2
2 2"><pre class="notranslate"><code>1 1
1 2
2 2
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Why?</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>thing_count</code> is a <em>class</em> variable</li>
<li>when a class is defined, Python creates a special "class" object that's <em>shared</em> by all instances of the class; it represents the <em>entire</em> class</li>
<li>so, we can think of <code>thing_count</code> as being "shared" across different instances of <code>Thing</code></li>
<li>we can access class (member) variables with the class name - like <code>Thing.thing_count += 1</code></li>
<li>in contrast, <code>self.value</code> is an <em>instance</em> (member) variable</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Class Method</h3><a id="user-content-class-method" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Class Method" href="#class-method"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Consider the following Python code with a class method, which has no <code>self</code> parameter:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class Thing:
 thing_count = 0

 def __init__(self, v):
  self.value = v
  Thing.thing_count += 1
  self.thing_num = Thing.thing_count


 def change_val(self, new_val):
  self.value = new_val

 def a_class_method(foo, bar):
  return Thing.thing_count * foo + bar

 def another_class_method(bletch):
  Thing.a_class_method(bletch,20)"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>:
 <span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>

 <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">v</span>):
  <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">value</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">v</span>
  <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_num</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span>


 <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">change_val</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">new_val</span>):
  <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">value</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">new_val</span>

 <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">a_class_method</span>(<span class="pl-s1">foo</span>, <span class="pl-s1">bar</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-s1">thing_count</span> <span class="pl-c1">*</span> <span class="pl-s1">foo</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-s1">bar</span>

 <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">another_class_method</span>(<span class="pl-s1">bletch</span>):
  <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-en">a_class_method</span>(<span class="pl-s1">bletch</span>,<span class="pl-c1">20</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>a_class_method</code> and <code>another_class_method</code> don't have a <code>self</code> parameter - so, they can't access instance (member) variables or functions!</p>
<p dir="auto">You can call them like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import thing

t1 = Thing(&quot;a&quot;)
Thing.another_class_method(42)"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">thing</span>

<span class="pl-s1">t1</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Thing</span>(<span class="pl-s">"a"</span>)
<span class="pl-v">Thing</span>.<span class="pl-en">another_class_method</span>(<span class="pl-c1">42</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">You generally want to use class methods and variables that only operate on state shared across the <em>entire</em> class (or have no state at all), and don't need any information about the instances.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Copying of Objects</h3><a id="user-content-copying-of-objects" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Copying of Objects" href="#copying-of-objects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Circle class in Python
import math

class Circle:

  def __init__(self, rad):
    self.rad = rad

  def area(self):
    return math.pi * self.rad**2

  def set_radius(self, rad):
    self.rad = rad"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Circle class in Python</span>
<span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">math</span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>:

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">area</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">math</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">*</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span><span class="pl-c1">**</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">set_radius</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">rad</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">rad</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">rad</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">What happens when we run this code?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="c = Circle(10)
print(c.area())
c2 = c
c.set_radius(0)
print(c2.area())  # What happens?!?!?"><pre><span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">area</span>())
<span class="pl-s1">c2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">c</span>
<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">set_radius</span>(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c2</span>.<span class="pl-en">area</span>())  <span class="pl-c"># What happens?!?!?</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer: prints <code>0</code>! This is a consequence of Python's ojbect reference behaviour. Assignment does not copy by default!</p>
<p dir="auto">But, we can implement our own copy implementation. One way to do this is with the <code>copy.deepcopy()</code> function:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import copy

c = Circle(10)
print(c.area())

c2 = copy.deepcopy(c)
c.set_radius(0)
print(c2.area) # not 0!"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">copy</span>

<span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Circle</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">area</span>())

<span class="pl-s1">c2</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">copy</span>.<span class="pl-en">deepcopy</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">c</span>.<span class="pl-en">set_radius</span>(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c2</span>.<span class="pl-s1">area</span>) <span class="pl-c"># not 0!</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">"Deep copying" recurisvely makes a copy of the top-level object, and <em>every</em> object it refers to.</p>
<p dir="auto">In contrast, shallow copying - done with <code>copy.copy()</code> - copies just the top level object (but not recursively).</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Automatic Garbage Collection</h3><a id="user-content-automatic-garbage-collection" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Automatic Garbage Collection" href="#automatic-garbage-collection"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">In Python, you don't have to worry about freeing objects when you're done with them, like you have to in C++. Instead, Python keeps track of who's pointing to each object; when nothing points to it, Python cleans it up.</p>
<p dir="auto">More broadly, this is called "automatic memory management".</p>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }
We'll cover this much more in-depth in the coming weeks!</p>
<p dir="auto">In other words: we don't need the <code>new</code> and <code>delete</code> keywords!</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Classes and Destructors</h3><a id="user-content-classes-and-destructors" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Classes and Destructors" href="#classes-and-destructors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Python has "destructors", but they're rarely used, and not guaranteed to run. More generally, they're really a type of "finalizer".</p>
<p dir="auto">It looks like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class TextBook:
  ...

class Student:
  def __init__(self):
    self.book = TextBook()

  def study(self):
    self.book.read()

  def __del__(self):
    if self.book.finished_reading():
      print(&quot;You graduated!&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">TextBook</span>:
  ...

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Student</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">book</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">TextBook</span>()

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">study</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">book</span>.<span class="pl-en">read</span>()

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__del__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">book</span>.<span class="pl-en">finished_reading</span>():
      <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">"You graduated!"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Destructors are only called when GC'd - but, it might not happen at all! Again, we'll explore this in a few lectures.</p>
<p dir="auto">(in Python, instead of having your destructor deal with non-memory resources - like temporary files, network connections, etc. - you'll want to explicitly free these)</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Inheritance</h3><a id="user-content-inheritance" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Inheritance" href="#inheritance"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">One key OOP feature is inheritance. Consider:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class Person:
  def __init__(self, name):
    self.name = name

  def talk(self):
    print('Hi!\n')

class Student(Person):
  def __init__(self, name):
    super().__init__(name)
    self.units = 0

  def talk(self):
    print(f&quot;Heya, I'm {self.name}.&quot;)
    print(&quot;Let's party! Oh... and &quot;)
    super().talk()"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Person</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">name</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">name</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">name</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">talk</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Hi!<span class="pl-cce">\n</span>'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Student</span>(<span class="pl-v">Person</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">name</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">super</span>().<span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">name</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">units</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">talk</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f"Heya, I'm <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">name</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>."</span>)
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">"Let's party! Oh... and "</span>)
    <span class="pl-en">super</span>().<span class="pl-en">talk</span>()</pre></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def chat(p):
 p.talk()

def cs131_lecture():
 s = Student('Angelina')
 chat(s)"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">chat</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>):
 <span class="pl-s1">p</span>.<span class="pl-en">talk</span>()

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">cs131_lecture</span>():
 <span class="pl-s1">s</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Student</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Angelina'</span>)
 <span class="pl-en">chat</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Some questions:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>How does a derived class inherit from a base class?</li>
<li>How does a derived class method override a base class method?</li>
<li>How does a derived method call a base-class method?</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answers:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>By placing the base class in the parens (e.g. <code>Student(Person)</code>)</li>
<li>"Virtual by default" - as long as they have the same name!</li>
<li>Using the <code>super()</code> prefix!</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto"><strong>You need to explicitly call the base class constructor!</strong></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Duck Typing</h3><a id="user-content-duck-typing" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Duck Typing" href="#duck-typing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Consider another classical pedagogical example:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class PersonInDuckSuit:
  ... 			  # code omitted for clarity
  def quack(self):
    print('Hi! Err... oops, I mean quack quack.')

class Duck:
  ... 			  # code omitted for clarity
  def quack(self):
    print('Quack quack quack!')

class Vehicle:
  ... 			  # code omitted for clarity
  def drive(self):
    print('Vrooooom!')"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">PersonInDuckSuit</span>:
  ... 			  <span class="pl-c"># code omitted for clarity</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">quack</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Hi! Err... oops, I mean quack quack.'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Duck</span>:
  ... 			  <span class="pl-c"># code omitted for clarity</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">quack</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Quack quack quack!'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">Vehicle</span>:
  ... 			  <span class="pl-c"># code omitted for clarity</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">drive</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Vrooooom!'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">What does this print?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def quack_please(x):
  x.quack()

p = PersonInDuckSuit()
d = Duck()
v = Vehicle()
quack_please(p)
quack_please(d)
quack_please(v)"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">quack_please</span>(<span class="pl-s1">x</span>):
  <span class="pl-s1">x</span>.<span class="pl-en">quack</span>()

<span class="pl-s1">p</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">PersonInDuckSuit</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">d</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Duck</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">v</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">Vehicle</span>()
<span class="pl-en">quack_please</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)
<span class="pl-en">quack_please</span>(<span class="pl-s1">d</span>)
<span class="pl-en">quack_please</span>(<span class="pl-s1">v</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Hi! Err... oops, I mean quack quack.
Quack quack quack!
AttributeError: 'Vehicle' object has no attribute 'quack'"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Hi! Err... oops, I mean quack quack.
Quack quack quack!
AttributeError: 'Vehicle' object has no attribute 'quack'
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This is a feature called <strong>duck typing</strong> - at runtime (and only when the line runs), Python checks if the input to <code>quack_please()</code> has a <code>quack</code> method. If it does, it runs that method; if not, an error is run.</p>
<p dir="auto">This is different from C++, which requires features like inheritance (or interfaces) to make this code works.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Object Equality</h3><a id="user-content-object-equality" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Object Equality" href="#object-equality"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">What does the following print?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Different types of equality in Python
fav = 'pizza'
a = f'I &lt;3 {fav}!'
b = f'I &lt;3 {fav}!'
c = a

if a == b:
  print('Both objects have same value!')
if c is a:
  print('c and a refer to the same obj')
if a is not b:
  print('a and b refer to diff. objs')"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Different types of equality in Python</span>
<span class="pl-s1">fav</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'pizza'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">f'I &lt;3 <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">fav</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>!'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">b</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">f'I &lt;3 <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">fav</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>!'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span>

<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-s1">b</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Both objects have same value!'</span>)
<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">is</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'c and a refer to the same obj'</span>)
<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">is</span> <span class="pl-c1">not</span> <span class="pl-s1">b</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'a and b refer to diff. objs'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Both objects have same value!
c and a refer to the same obj
a and b refer to diff. objs"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Both objects have same value!
c and a refer to the same obj
a and b refer to diff. objs
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Core ideas:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>==</code> looks at <em>values</em>, not references</li>
<li><code>is</code> looks at <em>references</em>, not values</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Object Identity</h3><a id="user-content-object-identity" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Object Identity" href="#object-identity"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Each distinct object has an ID number that we can access with the <code>id</code> function. For example,</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Different types of equality in Python
fav = 'pizza'
a = f'I &lt;3 {fav}!'
b = f'I &lt;3 {fav}!'
c = a

print(id(a)) # 140426129935136
print(id(b)) # 140426129649376
print(id(c)) # 140426129935136 -- the same!"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Different types of equality in Python</span>
<span class="pl-s1">fav</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">'pizza'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">f'I &lt;3 <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">fav</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>!'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">b</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s">f'I &lt;3 <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">fav</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>!'</span>
<span class="pl-s1">c</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span>

<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-en">id</span>(<span class="pl-s1">a</span>)) <span class="pl-c"># 140426129935136</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-en">id</span>(<span class="pl-s1">b</span>)) <span class="pl-c"># 140426129649376</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-en">id</span>(<span class="pl-s1">c</span>)) <span class="pl-c"># 140426129935136 -- the same!</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">{: .note }
In CPython (the reference Python implementation), <code>id()</code> returns the (virtual) memory address.</p>
<p dir="auto">Here's a challenge: are these object IDs going to be the same?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="booger = 10
print(id(booger))
booger = booger + 1
print(id(booger))"><pre><span class="pl-s1">booger</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">10</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-en">id</span>(<span class="pl-s1">booger</span>))
<span class="pl-s1">booger</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">booger</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-en">id</span>(<span class="pl-s1">booger</span>))</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Answer: no! Since, <code>10</code> and <code>11</code> have different addresses in memory! This is in contrast to C++, where the reference stays the same - the value at that memory just changes.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">None</h3><a id="user-content-none" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: None" href="#none"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Python has a keyword called <code>None</code>. Based on some code examples, what do you think it does?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def play_with_dog(lst):
  obj = None
  for x in lst:
    if x.is_canine():
      obj = x
      break
  if obj is not None:
    obj.give_bone()

def declare_happiness(what = None):
  if what is None:
    print(&quot;I'm happy for no reason!&quot;)
  else:
    print(f&quot;{what} makes me happy!&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">play_with_dog</span>(<span class="pl-s1">lst</span>):
  <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">x</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">lst</span>:
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">x</span>.<span class="pl-en">is_canine</span>():
      <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">x</span>
      <span class="pl-k">break</span>
  <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">is</span> <span class="pl-c1">not</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>:
    <span class="pl-s1">obj</span>.<span class="pl-en">give_bone</span>()

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">declare_happiness</span>(<span class="pl-s1">what</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">what</span> <span class="pl-c1">is</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>:
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">"I'm happy for no reason!"</span>)
  <span class="pl-k">else</span>:
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f"<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">what</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span> makes me happy!"</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We use <code>None</code> to indicate the absence of a value - it's like <code>nullptr</code> (in a way). The Pythonic way to validate if an item is/is not <code>None</code> is with the <code>is</code> and <code>is not</code> keywords.</p>
<p dir="auto">What do you think the following will do?</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="q = None

if q is False:
  print('Is None the same as False?')

if not q:
  print('Does not work with None?')

if q is None:
  print('Ahhh q is None!')

if q == None:
  print('Ahh q == None!')"><pre><span class="pl-s1">q</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>

<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">q</span> <span class="pl-c1">is</span> <span class="pl-c1">False</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Is None the same as False?'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-c1">not</span> <span class="pl-s1">q</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Does not work with None?'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">q</span> <span class="pl-c1">is</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Ahhh q is None!'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">q</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">None</span>:
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Ahh q == None!'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">...</p>
<p dir="auto">Answer:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="
Does not work with None?
Ahh q is None!
Ahh q == None!"><pre class="notranslate"><code>
Does not work with None?
Ahh q is None!
Ahh q == None!
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Importantly, <code>None</code> and <code>False</code> <em>aren't</em> exactly the same thing! But, it's "falsy" - which is why we get <code>if not q</code> working with <code>None</code>.</p>
